The Language of High-Fomorian

Natively known as: phómhóreígh phómóraigh /ˌpˠhoːmˠoːˈɾaɪ/ [ˌfˠhoːmˠoːˈɾaɪ]

...and he stood holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind...
uguß insíonn ér deaizíonn cemhpféir eans íhm uguß froelíonn édz amhúß eans íhm rei uguß insíonn ér diaezíonn cempféir eans íhmh uguß froillíonn édz amhúß eans íhm rei
Pronunciation: /ˈʊɟʊsˠ ɪɲˈʃiːɔnˠ eːɾ dʲaˈʒiːɔnˠ cemʲpʲfʲeːˈiɾ əu̯ŋsˠ iːhmʲ ˈʊɟʊsˠ fˠʁɔˈliːɔnˠ eːdʲʒ ˈamˠuːsˠ əu̯ŋsˠ iːhmʲ ɾaɪ̯/
Narrow pronunciation: [ˈʊɟʊsˠ ɪɲˈʃiːnˠ eːɾ dʲaˈʒiːnˠ cemʲpʲˈfʲeːɾ əu̯ŋsˠ iːhmʲ ˈʊɟʊsˠ fˠʁɔˈliːnˠ eːdʲʒ ˈamˠuːsˠ əu̯ŋsˠ iːhmʲ ʁaɪ̯]
High-Fomorian word order: and stood he holding his hat and turned his wet face to the wind

Grammar

Main word order: Verb Subject Object (Prepositional phrase). “Mary opened the door with a key” turns into Opened Mary the door with a key.
Adjective order: Adjectives are positioned before the noun.
Adposition: prepositions

High-Fomorian Orthography


High-Fomorian language has an alphabet only consisting of 15 consonants, but nearly as many vowels--13. This is largely due to the fact that High-Fomorian doesn't use all their vowels like we would. Instead, vowels denote how the consonant next to them should be pronounced, either broad or slender.

Initial Mutations

Lenition changes the way a letter is pronounced, and is shown by adding -h- after the initial letter of the word. In High-Fomorian, this occurs when the word is used in a specific way, or follows certain words. For example, the general article 'the'', as in 'the carr' or 'the woman', causes lenition in most words. Lenition is called séimhiú in High-Fomorian.
Another change that can occur to words in High-Fomorian is eclipsis. Like lenition, it is caused by the preceding word and it can effect both consonants and vowels (unlike lenition, which affects only consonants). Eclipsis is called urú in High-Fomorian. Eclipsis adds another letter that replaces the sound of the original letter. When you see the following combinations, pronounce the first letter and ignore the second -- it's left in place simply to show you what the word looked like before. Note that bh is considered a single letter!


Lenition

Normally, words beginning with the letters l, n , r are not changed. The following letters can be affected:
Letter Lenited Letter
bˠ h
k h
dˠ h
fˠ h
ɟ h
mˠ h
pˠ h
sˠ h
tˠ h
bʲ h
c h
dʲ h
fʲ h
g h
mʲ h
pʲ h
ʃ h
tʲ h
However, words beginning with sc-, sf-, sm-, sp-, and st- do not change.

Words beginning with an S are lenited only after an indefinite article.

Verbs

Present

Singular Plural
1st person The verb recieves an appropriate ending of -mʲ or -mˠ and also undergoes Lenition
chreaugamm chriaugamm /ˈchɾaʊ̯ɟamˠ/ [ˈçhɾaʊ̯ɟamˠ]
(I) walk
This verb conjugation remains unchanged from the infinitive.
criaugann criaugann /cɾaʊ̯ˈɟanˠ/
(we) walk
2nd person The verb recieves an appropriate ending of -ʃtʲ or -sˠtˠ and also undergoes Lenition
chreaugast chriaugast /ˈchɾaʊ̯ɟasˠtˠ/ [ˈçhɾaʊ̯ɟasˠtˠ]
(you) walk
The verb recieves an appropriate ending of -tʲ or -tˠ and also undergoes Eclipsis.
Criaugat gcreaugat /ˈgcɾaʊ̯ɟatˠ/ [ˈgɾaʊ̯ɟatˠ]
(you all) walk
3rd person The verb recieves an appropriate ending of -tʲ or -tˠ and also undergoes Lenition
chriaugat chriaugat /ˈchɾaʊ̯ɟatˠ/ [ˈçhɾaʊ̯ɟatˠ]
(he/she/it) walk
The verb does not recieve an ending, but undergoes Eclipsis.
Criaugann gcriaugann /gcɾaʊ̯ˈɟanˠ/ [gɾaʊ̯ˈɟanˠ]
(they) walk

Question Particles
Positive question Causes the verb to undergo Eclipsis following the particle: anˠ
an Eaurteann ann niaurteann /anˠ nʲaʊ̯ɾˈtʲəunˠ/
generic question particle
Negative question Causes the verb to undergo Eclipsis following the particle: nˠax
nach Iaurteann nach neaurteann /nˠax nʲaʊ̯ɾˈtʲəunˠ/
negative question particle
Negative statement Causes the verb to undergo Lenition following the particle: niː
ní aurteann ní aurteann /niː aʊ̯ɾˈtʲəunˠ/
negative verb particle

Numbers

High-Fomorian has a base-10 number system:

1 - zoel zoel
2 - lleug lleug
3 - ú ú
4 - grúnn grúnn
5 - llioer llioer
6 - zéi zé
7 - clú clú
8 - ceuest ceuist
9 - min min
10 - driua driua
11 - driua driuazoel zoel “ten-one”
100 - cá cá “hundred”
101 - cá cá zoill zoell “hundred one”
200 - lliug liug cá cá
1000 - Aeps naeps “thousand”

Derivational morphology

Verb → noun (the act of [verb]) = Particle before the undefined: ɟoː -
Adjective → noun (the quality of being [adj]) = Suffix -haɪtʲ
Noun → adjective (having the quality of [noun]) = Suffix -ɫʏ
One who [verb]s (e.g. paint → painter) = If ends with vowel: Suffix -tˠha
If ends with consonant: Change all Ctotˠha/C#
Diminutive = If ends with consonant: Suffix -einʲ|-iːnʲ|-aːnʲ
Else: Suffix -leinʲ|-tʲ
Augmentative = Suffix -aʊdˠ
Noun to verb = If ends with {pˠ,bˠ,fˠ,vˠ,mˠ,tˠ,dˠ,sˠ,nˠ,ʁ,ɫ,k,ɟ,x,h,ŋ,ʦ}: Suffix -aiːɔnˠ|-anˠ
If ends with {pʲ,bʲ,fʲ,vʲ,mʲ,tʲ,dʲ,ʃ,nʲ,ɾ,l,c,g,ç,h,ɲ,ʒ}: Suffix -əunˠ|-iːɔnˠ
If ends with {əu,e,ɪ,eː,iː,e,i,aɪ}: Suffix -ɔnˠ|-anˠ
If ends with {æː,oː,uː,ɛː,øː,ʏ,a,o,u}: Suffix -nˠaiːɔnˠ
Else: Suffix -iːɔnˠ
Verb → noun that verb produces (e.g. know → knowledge) = Particle before the undefined: bˠra -
Place of (e.g. wine → winery) = Suffix -ɾəu
Adjective → adverb = Suffix -iːg|aɪ
Adjective → verb (to make something [adj]) = Suffix -əunˠ
Noun → adjective relating to noun (e.g. economy → economic) = Suffix -ɪʃ
Tending to = Suffix -ɪç
Verb → adjective (result of doing [verb]) = Suffix -uː
